Eli Manning (MVP), 2 TDs Super Bowl 43: Ben Roethlisberger, 1 TD Super Bowl 44: Drew Brees (MVP), 2 TDs Super Bowl 45: Aaron Rogers (MVP), 3TDs Super Bowl 46: Eli Manning (MVP), 1 TD Super Bowl 47: Joe Flacco (MVP), 3TDs Super Bowl 48: Russell Wilson, 2TDs Super Bowl 49: Tom Brady (MVP), 4TDs Super Bowl 50: Peyton Manning, 0TDs Super Bowl 51: Tom Brady (MVP), 2TDs Super Bowl 52: Nick Foles (MVP), 3 TDs Super Bowl 53: Tom Brady, 0TDs Super Bowl 54: Patrick Mahomes (MVP), 2 TDs Super Bowl 55: Tom Brady (MVP), 3 TDs Super Bowl 56: Matthew Stafford, 3 TDs Super Bowl 57: Patrick Mahomes (MVP), 3 TDs Super Bowl 58: Patrick Mahomes (MVP), 2 TDs Super Bowl 59: Jalen Hurts (MVP), 2 TDs  A few repeat names in there, and don't forget to add the repeat names that also LOST a SB during this era too (Brady, Roethlisberger, Mahomes). What you wont see in this list, are the number of highly recruited 1st and 2nd round QB's drafted during this era, that have produced some decent seasons and playoff wins, but have yet to bring home a Lombardi. Deshaun Watson being the star of that list. Heisman winner, great athletic talent, and also the biggest bust and hugely overpaid by a front office that has no business running a front office. Do you think the other 31 teams have taken note and noticed a trend? Everyone wants notoriety and a bag of loot.   There may be some substance to Rich's claim, but it's more than just because of the Sanders' family attitude and approach. It took Matthew Stafford a whole career to win a SB... endured some painful seasons with injury, some painful to watch Lion's teams, but he's a warrior and managed to put up some good stats during that time too. Never once was he the highest paid QB, or darling of the NFL. Is Sheduer cut of that same kind of cloth? Highly doubtful. Is Joe Burrow? Is Brock Purdy? Justin Herbert? There's a whole list of active QB's that are proven to be ballers, but you gotta deliver that trophy. I don't see Sanders as one of those guys. Not even in the same ball park. The level of talent of Lamar Jackson and Josh Allen, with pretty good teams behind them, and still haven't reached their pinnacle. But, they still suit it up, take the hits, and masterfully deal with injury, BS media, and booing and hissing from their fanbases. Sanders isn't that guy...a little adversity and he'd fold like a cheap suit. And frankly, he's just not that talented. From a business view, the NFL sees him as a backup at best, and a backup that would just bring drama to the locker room. Add the Deshaun Watson contract debacle giving QB's a sense of inflated value, and here we are. This is a much bigger picture than these talking heads are willing to see and discuss.
